Mr. President, in 1918, the Spanish flu pandemic swept the world for a number of months with an outbreak in California that eventually took the lives of 30,000 of our fellow citizens. The flu spread so rapidly in the United States that public health officials said ``the days of scare mongering for the flu were over'' with outbreaks becoming more and more severe and contagious within the year. The strain in which it was found was one of the world's deadliest, with 2 million people dying in 1918 alone.  Fortunately for Americans, the pandemic began in Canada, where in December 1918, the Flu Pandemic Month, Canada hosted a smallpox vaccination for public health workers and their children. Mr. President, last November, the Drug Competition Act passed the Senate by unanimous consent. This bill would limit price increases in prescription drugs to 3 percent or less each year for 5 years and increase the marketing of generic drugs to the pharmaceutical industry by $1 billion a year for 5 years, whichever is greater.  Drug company profits rose significantly during the first 4 years of the Drug Competition Act as drug manufacturers reported higher sales, higher profits, and added significantly to the compensation of their top executives. Final sequence: 

Mr. Chairman, I would like to explain the content and purpose of this amendment, which would provide the funds needed to support a recently established program within the Department of Energy for the purpose of assisting private entities in developing alternative fuels for electric vehicles. This program is called the Projects for Competitive Alternatives for Electric Vehicles program. It would allow private companies such as GM and Chrysler to have access to a competitive and limited private sector funding stream for investing in research and development of new electric vehicle technologies. This grant would encourage more than 35 companies to develop these innovative programs within the next year to generate billions of dollars in private sector investments and jobs.
